  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6b4e5853-41be-4801-8ecb-2a4cbc626f8b'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText16849335025107428756" style="display:none">Do twins begin in the womb?<br />Or in a better place?<br /><br />Kaeleigh and Raeanne are identical down to the dimple. As daughters of a district-court judge father and a politician mother, they are an all-American family—on the surface. Behind the facade each sister has her own dark secret, and that's where their differences begin.<br /><br />For Kaeleigh, she's the misplaced focus of Daddy's love, intended for a mother whose presence on the campaign trail means absence at home. All that Raeanne sees is Daddy playing a game of favorites—and she is losing. If she has to lose, she will do it on her own terms, so she chooses drugs, alcohol, and sex.<br /><br />Secrets like the ones the twins are harboring are not meant to be kept—from each other or anyone else. Pretty soon it's obvious that neither sister can handle it alone, and one sister must step up to save the other, but the question is—who?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71245344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6706735805796071324"><b>Posted at <a href='http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2015/09/identical.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelf Inflicted</a></b><br/><br/>My grandfather was a prick. He was an alcoholic and a gambler. He had anger issues and extreme mood swings. He was liberal with his money at the race track and when he was out drinking with his buddies, but it was a big deal if my grandmother wanted a new dress or my mom needed a new pair of shoes. I always hated the way he treated my grandmother and my mother and hated the way they behaved when they were around him. I hated visiting my grandparents on Sundays after chur</span>
  <span id="freeText6706735805796071324" style="display:none"><b>Posted at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2015/09/identical.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a></b><br /><br />My grandfather was a prick. He was an alcoholic and a gambler. He had anger issues and extreme mood swings. He was liberal with his money at the race track and when he was out drinking with his buddies, but it was a big deal if my grandmother wanted a new dress or my mom needed a new pair of shoes. I always hated the way he treated my grandmother and my mother and hated the way they behaved when they were around him. I hated visiting my grandparents on Sundays after church and especially hated being left alone with my grandfather. He died peacefully in his sleep at the age of 86. It was too good for him. <br /> <br />Though I had no reservations about reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69024079" rel="nofollow noopener">Tricks</a>, some of the issues in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2241059.Identical" title="Identical by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Identical</a> were a little too close to home for me, and I was afraid of triggering unwanted memories. My fear cast aside, I decided to borrow the unabridged audio version from the library. While my vague memories remained far in the past, I was able to feel a deep emotional connection with the characters. Ellen Hopkins must have teenagers of her own, or is very knowledgeable about the problems that can affect them. Her characters are solid, believable, and strong. As much as I enjoyed the narration, I find that the author's intimate writing style and loosely constructed free prose is meant to be read. After listening to the audio version, I borrowed the book just to see how the 16-year-old identical twins, Kaeleigh's and Raeanne's thoughts were shaped. <br /> <br />The story is told in alternating perspectives by the twins and covers myriad teenage problems, including father-daughter incest, eating disorders, drug abuse, mental illness, promiscuity, and cutting. While the characters were easy to get to know, I found the issues covered a bit too overwhelming and excessive foreshadowing revealed a plot twist that was not a big surprise to me by the book's conclusion. <br /> <br />Still, a mostly satisfying read and I look forward to Hopkins' other titles. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6706735805796071324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147028226?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147028226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3121328227796542975">This book was... disturbing. Very disturbing. I really like the author's style and I think the use of verse is highly effective and contributes something to the story that I never imagined possible... but. And there is a but. I felt this book, unlike Burned which I loved, just went too far. It made me feel uncomfortable, too much so. I can't explain, I usually really like books that are controversial and stretch boundaries but... a man performing oral sex on his daughter while her twin watched a</span>
  <span id="freeText3121328227796542975" style="display:none">This book was... disturbing. Very disturbing. I really like the author's style and I think the use of verse is highly effective and contributes something to the story that I never imagined possible... but. And there is a but. I felt this book, unlike Burned which I loved, just went too far. It made me feel uncomfortable, too much so. I can't explain, I usually really like books that are controversial and stretch boundaries but... a man performing oral sex on his daughter while her twin watched and secretly wished it was her? The revulsion I felt was too much. Way too much.<br /><br />I thought the plot idea was great, very interesting and a rather dangerous subject area to delve into (child abuse, amongst other things). Basically, it's the story of identical twins, almost completely alike except one is the reluctant centre of her father's attention... sexual attention. The other twin feels unloved by her father and longs to please him... even sexually. That was the part of this book that made my stomach churn, not so much the abuse of one twin but the incestuous desires of the other. <br /><br />I read it in a few hours and was gripped in a manner that can only be described as 'horrified'. I couldn't put it down, like the inability to look away from a road accident even after seeing a mangled body. Perhaps it should be given more stars, but I didn't really <i>enjoy</i> this book. Who knows? I'll probably read it again in the future and I might decide to revise this rating. We shall see.</span>

<div id="review_45967228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45967228" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45967228?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">More mature teens</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Thomas by: </span>
      Read "Impulse" and decided to pick up this one
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45967228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11833632141096634359">I have to say, this book is pretty amazing.<br/><br/>Basically it's about these two twins, Kaeleigh and Raeanne. They are half of the All-American family, with a dad who is a judge and a mom who is running for a position in Congress. But what lies beneath their facade is really dysfunction; and the worst, worst kind.<br/><br/>Kaeleigh, the introverted one, is being sexually abused by Ray, her own father, and also binges and cuts herself. Raeanne is the exact opposite and is more outgoing, but finds herself wanting </span>
  <span id="freeText11833632141096634359" style="display:none">I have to say, this book is pretty amazing.<br /><br />Basically it's about these two twins, Kaeleigh and Raeanne. They are half of the All-American family, with a dad who is a judge and a mom who is running for a position in Congress. But what lies beneath their facade is really dysfunction; and the worst, worst kind.<br /><br />Kaeleigh, the introverted one, is being sexually abused by Ray, her own father, and also binges and cuts herself. Raeanne is the exact opposite and is more outgoing, but finds herself wanting the attention Kaeleigh always gets. So, she resorts to drugs, and lots, and lots of sex. And this is just the beginning of the horrible suffering the twins face in this book.<br /><br />As a teenager myself, I must admit that sometimes I cringed while reading the book and had to put it down for a second. However, I would immediately pick it right back up and continue reading. I strongly would recommend not giving this book out to teens under the age of 14; it's just THAT graphic at some parts of the story. Not bad, though.<br /><br />Ellen Hopkin's unique poetry style is commanding and flawlessly executed, and when the twin's viewpoint switches over the mirroring effect is awe-inspiring. (read the individual words as they go down the page.)<br /><br />The twist at the end was... wow. I remember the shock I experienced the first time I saw it. Overall, if you are a fan of Ellen Hopkin's previous works this will be another amazing read through, if not, then it won't hurt to give it a try. /end review</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7874519783332704429"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>This book was amazing and it tore me apart :( I had a feeling I knew where it was going and it did but in a little bit of a different way. But it will be put back together. <br><br>This is a brilliantly sad story and I will continue on with all of the author's books I have yet to read. <br><br><a href="http://s1379.photobucket.com/user/melmartD11/media/book%20banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <span id="freeText7555605100055853222" style="display:none">I'm struggling on what to rate this book its between 2 and 3 stars. I guess I'll give it a 2.5. It's a lot. First and foremost there are A LOT of triggers in this book, sexual abuse, cutting, addiction, eating disorders, mental illness. It's a lot to take in and it's a struggle to get through. Anyone who wants to read this book I reccomend going into it with causation because it is so heavy and deep. I really like Ellen Hopkins and I think shes a very talented author and she does talk about subjects most people wont because they're very difficult, but this book was just to much. I honestly don't really know what else to say about it. If it wasn't written in verse I wouldn't have gotten through it. The writing style is the only thing that saved his book for me.</span>

<div id="review_46359558" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46359558" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1740420-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603987270p2/1740420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46359558?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/1740420-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1740420-christina?shelf=source-library">source-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1740420-christina?shelf=2009-reads">2009-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1740420-christina?shelf=genre-fiction">genre-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer46359558&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46359558" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16780089748453369289">Identical takes on the issue of sexual abuse by a relative. In this case, Kaeleigh is sexually abused by her father while her twin sister, Raeanne, isn’t. Raeanne never tells on her father, especially since her mother is distant {she’s running for Congress} and cold. And the story, written in the same free verse Hopkins used in Crank and Glass, switches from the point of view of Kaeleigh to Raeanne. Of occasionally, if you follow the sepearate words down the page, the girls come to the same conc</span>
  <span id="freeText16780089748453369289" style="display:none">Identical takes on the issue of sexual abuse by a relative. In this case, Kaeleigh is sexually abused by her father while her twin sister, Raeanne, isn’t. Raeanne never tells on her father, especially since her mother is distant {she’s running for Congress} and cold. And the story, written in the same free verse Hopkins used in Crank and Glass, switches from the point of view of Kaeleigh to Raeanne. Of occasionally, if you follow the sepearate words down the page, the girls come to the same conclusion through different experiences and sometimes they repeat what one another has to say.<br /><br /> “At ten, it isn’t exactly<br /> easy to separate<br /> good touch<br /> from bad<br /> touch,<br /> proper<br /> love from<br /> improper love,<br /> doting daddy from perv.” {pg. 241}<br /><br />When I started my review in my head towards the end of Identical, I was all set to complain about how indistinguishable Kaeleigh is from Raeanne and visa versa. The identical twins I know are completely distinguishable - in dress, mannerism, and voice. Raeanna and Kaeleigh are not, and I found myself flipping back and forth, back and forth between the pages to make sure who I thought was speaking was, in fact, speaking. But then I reached the end and my complaint was explained. At least, to a degree.<br /><br />You see, the ending in unexpected, unexplainable, and completely out there. At the end of the book, you learn that Raeanna actually died in the car accident caused by Ray and Kaeleigh has multiple identities, living through herself and her twin sister to cope with the sexual abuse. Now that I think about it, the book is riddled with clues: Raeanne and Kaeleigh never talk to one another, the accident Ray caused never made any sense, the fact that Madison hits on both girls’ boyfriends, why Ray would choose one daughter over the other when they’re supposed to be identical. But the ending didn’t settle right with me; it felt too much like a copout.<br /><br />And the fact that, rather than focus on one issue, Hopkins threw in sexual abuse, bondage, teacher-student relationships, parents’ separation, rape, child p*rnography, pr*stitution, drags, and alcohol abuse. I don’t know if she was trying (too hard} to be “edge” and push the envelop with her novel or if she couldn’t decide which problem to focus on in this novel, but her jam packed novel didn’t settle right with me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16780089748453369289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6833815858289815411">I can certainly say that this is one of my favorite books now. In the beginning, I couldn't help but to think what the ending would be like. It never really gives you a sure-fire conflict. I mean, yes, one twin is molested by her father. The other is getting into a lot of trouble with drugs and boys. But while reading it, the whole time I thought maybe their problems would resolve themselves. Once I got to the ending everything made sense to me and I couldn't help but to stare at my wall for a f</span>
  <span id="freeText6833815858289815411" style="display:none">I can certainly say that this is one of my favorite books now. In the beginning, I couldn't help but to think what the ending would be like. It never really gives you a sure-fire conflict. I mean, yes, one twin is molested by her father. The other is getting into a lot of trouble with drugs and boys. But while reading it, the whole time I thought maybe their problems would resolve themselves. Once I got to the ending everything made sense to me and I couldn't help but to stare at my wall for a few minutes with my mouth wide open. It was THAT surprising of an ending. I really had no idea that it would be THAT huge. I think I need to re-read it. Just to give myself more of an understanding now that I know what happened. I never want to re-read a book straight after finishing it. I also have to say, I've never read something in this style or with such plot. I wish I could give this book 1000/10 stars. I honestly do. Read this book. The poetry isn't too difficult to read. It's written prose-y and you can certainly read it like a real book once you get by it's format. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2090381101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16079050462489092100"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I doubt I'll ever cotton to the literary stylings of Ellen Hopkins (that faux-poetry thing drives me nuts; she's no Jacqueline Woodson, that's for damn sure) but I suspect <b>Identical</b> will strike a chord of truth for incest survivors and others who've grown up in exceedingly dysfuctional families like the one that identical twin sisters Kaeleigh and Raeanne endure here. About as subtle as unanesthetized oral surgery, and (for me, anyway) just as painful to endure.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27522484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27522484" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27522484?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27522484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15220298788319140664">Okay so, WOW. I was first introduced to the power of verse writing when I read I Heart You, You Haunt Me by Lisa Schroeder. I love the rawness, no fluffy descriptions or unneeded stances, just pure emotion. Laci is a huge fan of Ellen Hopkins and she had been trying to get me to read one of her books for a long time. And it isn’t that I didn’t want to, I was just waiting for the right opportunity. And when opportunity comes knockin, you best answer the door.<br/><br/>I read a lot of books. And ones that m</span>
  <span id="freeText15220298788319140664" style="display:none">Okay so, WOW. I was first introduced to the power of verse writing when I read I Heart You, You Haunt Me by Lisa Schroeder. I love the rawness, no fluffy descriptions or unneeded stances, just pure emotion. Laci is a huge fan of Ellen Hopkins and she had been trying to get me to read one of her books for a long time. And it isn’t that I didn’t want to, I was just waiting for the right opportunity. And when opportunity comes knockin, you best answer the door.<br /><br />I read a lot of books. And ones that make a definite impression are few and far between. But I’m not always in the mood to read a book that makes an “impression” sometimes I just want a book that entertains me, makes me feel good. Identical falls in the former category with a few other books that continue to stay on my mind.<br /><br />This book is engrossing, it’s disturbing, it’s disgusting, it’s addictive, it’s powerful and I loved it. I did have sneaking suspicion throughout the entire book and when it was finally revealed I still didn’t believe it. But, the less you know about that going in, the better. Now that I’ve read Identical, I know I won’t be able to stop, I’ll have to read Hopkins earlier titles and continue to read her new ones. And a fan is born.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15220298788319140664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8389571395350299329">One family - damaged by tragedy. A father who drinks too much; an absentee, professionally-driven mother. Twin girls left in the middle. <br/><br/>Kaeleigh and Raeanne are identical twins - each with their own deep, dark secret. One daughter attracts the inappropriate attention of their damaged father. The other daughter, usually ignored, takes part in riskier and riskier behavior just screaming to be heard.   <span id="freeText8389571395350299329" style="display:none">One family - damaged by tragedy. A father who drinks too much; an absentee, professionally-driven mother. Twin girls left in the middle. <br /><br />Kaeleigh and Raeanne are identical twins - each with their own deep, dark secret. One daughter attracts the inappropriate attention of their damaged father. The other daughter, usually ignored, takes part in riskier and riskier behavior just screaming to be heard. Both girls suffer in silence, living behind the facade of a perfect, all-American family.<br /><br />Ellen Hopkins has written another gripping novel in verse that will leave you on the edge of your seat. If you are at all familiar with her work you know to expect the unexpected. Prepare for your jaw to drop when you reach the end of this gripping tale. You absolutely won’t believe your eyes.<br /><br />Be aware - this is a graphic story. I have Crank in my middle school library, but I WOULD NOT have this one available to them. It is HEAVY!!</span>

<div id="review_33409924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33409924" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/377085-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203195126p2/377085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33409924?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/377085-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Hopkins fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377085-debbie?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377085-debbie?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377085-debbie?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377085-debbie?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377085-debbie?shelf=drugs-and-alcohol">drugs-and-alcohol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377085-debbie?shelf=eating-disorders">eating-disorders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377085-debbie?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33409924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15129335468343471825">Kaeleigh and Raeanne are identical twins, mirror images of each other. They share a terrible secret. <br/><br/>Kaeleigh is the good girl--she does well in school and has a lead role in the school musical. Ian, her sort-of boyfriend, loves her deeply. Her father loves her too, but not the way a father should.<br/><br/>Raeanne knows about her father's visits to Kaeleigh's bed. While a part of her wants to protect Kaeleigh, another part of her feels jealous because her father didn't pick her. She breaks rules at every</span>
  <span id="freeText15129335468343471825" style="display:none">Kaeleigh and Raeanne are identical twins, mirror images of each other. They share a terrible secret. <br /><br />Kaeleigh is the good girl--she does well in school and has a lead role in the school musical. Ian, her sort-of boyfriend, loves her deeply. Her father loves her too, but not the way a father should.<br /><br />Raeanne knows about her father's visits to Kaeleigh's bed. While a part of her wants to protect Kaeleigh, another part of her feels jealous because her father didn't pick her. She breaks rules at every turn, skipping school, getting high, and having all kinds of sex. <br /><br />The family was normal until the night of the accident, when their father, a judge, caused a fatal accident while driving drunk. Their mother responded by throwing herself into her political career and freezing out her family. Their parents are still married, but the marriage is in name only. <br /><br />Their father, lonely and tortured by his own terrible secret, drinks to escape his demons. And he sexually abuses Kaeleigh. <br /><br />I loved the format of the novel. The poems were beautifully written and the shapes, especially of the mirrored ones, made me slow down and savor the structure.<br /><br />The treatment of Raeanne's drug use made me a bit uncomfortable, mostly because the negative aspects were downplayed. In Crank, which details a girl's downward spiral into addiction, her drug use is also graphic and descriptive, but the reader could clearly see the path of destruction. <br /><br />I would have liked to have read more about Kaeleigh's relationship with her father and also about the events in his childhood that set him on the path of the abuser. Also, the twist at the end would have felt more authentic if it hadn't happened so close to the end of the book. I wanted to know more about what happened AFTER Kaeleigh faced the truth. <br /><br />While this was not my favorite Hopkins novel, teen fans will not be able to put it down. It is chock full of issues and mature content. It's all here--sexual abuse, drug and alcohol abuse, eating disorders, cutting, mental illness, bad boys, and, like Pandora's box, a small taste of hope and love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15129335468343471825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19756585" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19756585" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/244267-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332624023p2/244267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19756585?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/244267-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/244267-caroline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/244267-caroline?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19756585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7470577136126821999">This is one of those really hard books to review, because it's difficult to say if I really enjoyed it. It deals with twin sisters, one who is sexually abused by their father for years and the other who watches it from her bed.<br/><br/>It's a story dealing with sexual abuse, mental illness, drug abuse, alcoholism, eating disorders and promiscuity in teenagers, and at times it was really horrifying and difficult to read. But, Ellen Hopkins is really excellent at pulling you through the tough spots with so</span>
  <span id="freeText7470577136126821999" style="display:none">This is one of those really hard books to review, because it's difficult to say if I really enjoyed it. It deals with twin sisters, one who is sexually abused by their father for years and the other who watches it from her bed.<br /><br />It's a story dealing with sexual abuse, mental illness, drug abuse, alcoholism, eating disorders and promiscuity in teenagers, and at times it was really horrifying and difficult to read. But, Ellen Hopkins is really excellent at pulling you through the tough spots with some kind of glimmer of hope that things might turn out alright in the end.<br /><br />At first I hated the sheer number of names Hopkins dumps on the reader right at the beginning--the book is separated into chunks (basically, chapters, but Hopkins doesn't really ever use chapters in her novels) told from the perspective of each twin, with a neat mirror effect with the poetry every time the perspective swaps. There's a lot of names, though, and at first I had a tough time keeping it all straight. By the end it was definitely worth it.<br /><br />I was bugged by some of the details, like the fact the sisters never really interact with each other even though they <i>see</i> each other. Luckily, this is resolved in the end in a way I was expecting about halfway through but was still surprised to see her pull off.<br /><br />It definitely kept me reading, despite some of the rougher points. On sheer craft, plot and character I'd probably have rated this 5-stars, but I certainly can't claim to have loved this. "Liked it" is the closest I can get--I'm glad I read it, but it's really hard for me to really say how much I enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7470577136126821999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2150644007" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2150644007" />
    <a title="Rikke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13002095-rikke"><img alt="Rikke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448272410p2/13002095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2150644007?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rikke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rikke" href="/user/show/13002095-rikke">Rikke</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781416984658" href="/book/show/7013295-identical">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13002095-rikke?shelf=great-contemporary">great-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13002095-rikke?shelf=5-stars-2017">5-stars-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13002095-rikke?shelf=great-uncomfy">great-uncomfy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150644007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6588752255608646856">This story is so disturbing I'm almost appalled at myself for enjoying it this much. The writing is great though, and the story too actually. Awesome really. I thought I knew what I was reading, and then she flipped it. Quite brilliantly. I should have thought of it. I loved that I didn't. It's so lovely to be oblivious. No, really. I usually expect plot twists, and I mostly find it tiring if there are none. Just not with this genre. Probably because it's just light, bland, nothingness most of t</span>
  <span id="freeText6588752255608646856" style="display:none">This story is so disturbing I'm almost appalled at myself for enjoying it this much. The writing is great though, and the story too actually. Awesome really. I thought I knew what I was reading, and then she flipped it. Quite brilliantly. I should have thought of it. I loved that I didn't. It's so lovely to be oblivious. No, really. I usually expect plot twists, and I mostly find it tiring if there are none. Just not with this genre. Probably because it's just light, bland, nothingness most of the time. At least IMO more often than not, it's time wasted. <br /><br />And then this book comes along. Really, why is it that I automatically disregard contemporary fiction? I know... Because it doesn't interest me much. Because they're all the same.. Identical is more, though. It's teenage drama and family life, sure, but not just. And not just small ridiculous stuff, or a bunch of generic morals being pushed through either. <br /><br />This novel offers more than mere ordinary or relatable issues. It probably won't make you feel, like you've experienced something similar, or know someone who has. It might not even make you feel all that emotional - except maybe more or less appalled - regardless of the devastating subject. Or, I wouldn't think so. At least I didn't love it for its ability to draw me in emotionally. I loved it as a whole, especially because it allows for a lot more grayscale than most. <br /><br />Which I think, is what makes it stand out. That, and the fact that nothing gets sugarcoated, or gloss over. Also it's the definitely proof, that there's still lots of great stories, I've missed. <br /><br />In fact, I might just have to go back to screening the contemporary genre a bit more thoroughly. Maybe even read the actual description rather than just skim a few lines. And acknowledge, that the genre is not all chick-lit, teenage romance and the likes. At least not if I'm more careful with my choices. <br /><br />I've actually been wanting to read something by Ellen Hopkins for awhile. I can't recall why though, because if had I known what to expect, I wouldn't have left it for sometime in the future. <br /><br />Obvious I'm happy with this book. It's one of a small number of books I've actually liked enough to go for the five star rating this year. *Sad face* <br /><br />As for Ellen Hopkins. I'm definitely reading more of her books. Soon. Fortunately there is a lot of them. <br /><br />In fact I went straight on to RUMBLE. Which I enjoyed less - Probably inevitable, because how would it compare to this one? And it's kind of impossible not to compare, when reading them back to back. So the next one will be as soon as I've read a few non-contemporaries.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6588752255608646856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer845592840273636813">(spoiler)<br/><br/>Honestly, I was a little surprised by this book. I'm used to her books being about drugs or sexual things, but this book was different. At the beginning you're introduced to these two twin sisters, Kaeleigh and Raeanne. You learn that their father sexually abuses Kaeleigh and Raeanne secretly wants it.<br/><br/>Then you LATER learn, Kaeleigh's mother never forgave their father for the car accident he caused in which Raeanna died & the mother was injured.   <span id="freeText845592840273636813" style="display:none">(spoiler)<br /><br />Honestly, I was a little surprised by this book. I'm used to her books being about drugs or sexual things, but this book was different. At the beginning you're introduced to these two twin sisters, Kaeleigh and Raeanne. You learn that their father sexually abuses Kaeleigh and Raeanne secretly wants it.<br /><br />Then you LATER learn, Kaeleigh's mother never forgave their father for the car accident he caused in which Raeanna died &amp; the mother was injured. The mother, Kay, then ran for Congress woman and was never home, which made the fater, Ray, in charge of everything. The daughters both had their major problems: drugs, sex, alcohol, etc. and they both had a hard time loving someone else after what their father did to them.<br /><br />The sad part is, at the end of the book, or near the end of the book I should say, you learn that Raeanna actually died in the car accident caused by Ray and Kaeleigh had multiple identities, living through herself and her twin sister.<br /><br />It was a really confusing book and makes me wonder where Ellen Hopkins gets her ideas, you know? I was a little disappointed, but it was an okay book, it kept me reading. Ellen could have done a lot better though.</span>

<div id="review_779385149" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779385149" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590065910p2/6504379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/779385149?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=ya-read">ya-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779385149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8550764633023062697">For the last several days since I finished <i>Identical</i>, I, A. have been trying to think of how best to review this first Ellen Hopkins read for me, and B. I keep finding myself thinking about Kaleigh and Raeanne and their stories. Oh, and I guess a C....Well, I've already ordered two more of Hopkins' books, and bought two at Half-Price Books. :)<br/><br/>Having never read Ellen Hopkins, nor a book written in poetry form, I was skeptical if I would like the style or not. My friend Janie recently read <i>Identic</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8550764633023062697" style="display:none">For the last several days since I finished <i>Identical</i>, I, A. have been trying to think of how best to review this first Ellen Hopkins read for me, and B. I keep finding myself thinking about Kaleigh and Raeanne and their stories. Oh, and I guess a C....Well, I've already ordered two more of Hopkins' books, and bought two at Half-Price Books. :)<br /><br />Having never read Ellen Hopkins, nor a book written in poetry form, I was skeptical if I would like the style or not. My friend Janie recently read <i>Identical</i> and thought I would like it, and her review really made me want to check this out for myself. I found the book used, and was really excited to get it. When I finally did receive it in the mail, I finished up my current read at the time, and moved this up on my reading list. I am so glad I did that.....<br /><br />What a powerful (not necessarily in the way you might think), emotional, crazy, unbelievable story. I have never read anything quite like this before, and it was extremely refreshing. <br /><br />Now, even though I said I've never read anything quite like <i>Identical</i>, I have read books about drug use, promiscuous sex, alcohol abuse, and the like. And to be honest, they are usually some of the best books I've read and my favorites. I don't know why and am unsure of what that says about me. It sounds bad to say, almost, because I find it fascinating, intriguing, and I even like the heart-breaking things to some extent. I like rooting for these characters you wouldn't root for in real life. I love feeling SOMETHING. <br /><br />Ellen Hopkins and <i>Identical</i> made me feel A LOT. I love when an author can do this to me. I kept wanting certain things to happen I wouldn't have wanted my own daughter, of which I don't have kids, doing. To me, that is part of what makes this book so good. <br /><br />What also made this book so good is the fact, in the beginning, I had a slight suspicion of what was really going on. But, Hopkins really took that idea away from me and made me abandon it. Then, when I found out what was really going on, I couldn't believe I didn't see it coming sooner. My original idea was wrong for the most part, and I like that I was wrong. <br /><br />Oh, and do I even need to say there is some F&amp;@%!* UP!!!!, crazy stuff in this story. I'm sorry to use language like that, but this is serious. I had suspected a part of what was going on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the dad raping his daughter continuously <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But when Raeanne says, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she wishes she could love Daddy better than Kaeleigh, and basically she would give him sex whenever he wanted and however he wanted <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. OMG. OMG. I had to walk away from the book for a moment. <br /><br />And even though I had to walk away, I still had to know what was going on. To me, that is so important to me about writing, but also, it's what I love and why I read. <br /><br />Ellen Hopkins is surely not an author to miss. I don't think many people can handle her books (well, I've only read this one, but they follow the same type of destructive lives), so I definitely say proceed with caution. All in all, a fantastic, refreshing read, and I am really, really looking forward to reading the rest of her work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8550764633023062697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_361517624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/361517624" />
    <a title="✿.Ⓐⓟⓞⓞⓡⓥⓐ.✿" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10700747"><img alt="✿.Ⓐⓟⓞⓞⓡⓥⓐ.✿" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409179932p2/10700747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/361517624?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✿.Ⓐⓟⓞⓞⓡⓥⓐ.✿" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✿.Ⓐⓟⓞⓞⓡⓥⓐ.✿" href="/user/show/10700747">✿.Ⓐⓟⓞⓞⓡⓥⓐ.✿</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361517624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16107092794338369960"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380382888ra/740966.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let me start by saying that when I read a book, I am usually certain about whether or not I liked it. However, that is not the case with this book. "Identical" is the first book I have read by Ellen Hopkins, and I'm very unsure what to think, or if I want to read any of her other books.<br/><br/>I have never particularly enjoyed verse writing, so when this book arrived and I saw that it was ALL in verse, I considered just leaving it in a corner to collect dust. BUT! Yes, there's a "but". After reading a c</span>
  <span id="freeText16107092794338369960" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380382888ra/740966.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me start by saying that when I read a book, I am usually certain about whether or not I liked it. However, that is not the case with this book. "Identical" is the first book I have read by Ellen Hopkins, and I'm very unsure what to think, or if I want to read any of her other books.<br><br>I have never particularly enjoyed verse writing, so when this book arrived and I saw that it was ALL in verse, I considered just leaving it in a corner to collect dust. BUT! Yes, there's a "but". After reading a couple reviews on here, I decided to give it a shot. I can say that I'm glad I did.<br><br>Now I know since you're reading this, you have probably heard all about the book from the summary and all the other reviews. So I won't talk about that at all. There are a couple things I would like to say though.<br><br>1) People who say this book is too disturbing: Don't listen. I'm a young reader, and I PROMISE you it did not corrupt me in any way. If not the best book in the world, the story is one that teaches us a lot about ourselves. Though I myself don't do drugs or go around sleeping with every guy I meet (let out that breath you've been holding), I find that the emotions are very easy to relate to.<br><br><br><br>2) *SPOILER HERE (kinda)*: I wish that Kaeleigh had told Ian about her father, or at least that he had found out some other way.<br><br>3) *REAL SPOILER*: I was SO shocked when I found out that Raeanne was dead. At the end, Kaeleigh feels more in control. However, I just felt hopeless from the perspective of a reader. Sure, Kaeleigh learns to stand up for herself. But come on. She lost her sister, her twin sister, her strongest link. The fact that I'm frustrated probably means that Ellen Hopkins did her job though.<br><br><br><br>So should you read this book? Sure. Give it a go. If you're like me and can't abandon a book, you'll be fine. It's a quickie. But don't expect something amazing. And the "disgusting" parts... embrace them for their part in the story. It's life, and there is no use hiding from it. I commend Hopkins for being brave enough to express this issue as it is. If people have a problem with it, then they can read a whole lot of other books out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16107092794338369960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3387625693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3387625693" />
    <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes"><img alt="aPriL does feral sometimes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478243665p2/3409532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3387625693?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416950066" href="/book/show/7775706-identical">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=illuminating">illuminating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=a-jack-in-the-box-pop-surprise">a-jack-in-the-box-pop-surprise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=very-very-disturbing-to-me">very-very-disturbing-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=unbearably-sad">unbearably-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=older-teen">older-teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3387625693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8598782792972439907">''Identical' by Ellen Hopkins tackles a very difficult subject. A father decides his nine-year-old daughter will be great to have sex with whenever he wants sex. So, eight years after the abuse started, Kaeleigh is still the perfect daughter to him. She never says no to him. In fact, she apologizes to him. A lot. He reminds her she has to be clean and neat at all times. Sometimes she isn't. He must know where she is at all times. He demands respect. After all, he's a district court judge.<br/><br/>Where i</span>
  <span id="freeText8598782792972439907" style="display:none">''Identical' by Ellen Hopkins tackles a very difficult subject. A father decides his nine-year-old daughter will be great to have sex with whenever he wants sex. So, eight years after the abuse started, Kaeleigh is still the perfect daughter to him. She never says no to him. In fact, she apologizes to him. A lot. He reminds her she has to be clean and neat at all times. Sometimes she isn't. He must know where she is at all times. He demands respect. After all, he's a district court judge.<br /><br />Where is Kaeleigh's mother? She is in Washington, D.C. - a long way from the California valley where Kaeleigh and her father live. She is a congresswoman. At the moment, she is running for re-election. But either way, when in California for a visit or gone for months, she no longer cares about Kaeleigh. She hasn't since the car accident. Kaeleigh's daddy is an alcoholic and was driving drunk with his wife and twin girls, Kaeleigh and Raeanne. It was a terrible accident. Nothing was ever the same. But publicly? They are a happy family.<br /><br />Raeanne and Kaeleigh know the family is a dysfunctional mess. But neither can see a way out except for one way. Kaeleigh is a good student and works at a nursing home after school, but she gets high on marijuana to do it. Raeanne trades sex for drugs. Both drink too. <br /><br />It's ok, it seems to work. It stops the emotional pain, plus it is so much fun. They both know love is fake, love doesn't exist, so in not caring about love, they don't need it. They are both cool, doing well. Daddy takes care of them, and Kaeleigh takes care of daddy. Raeanne is jealous, but she is having sex with a lot of older guys in trade for drugs. It is working. But why can't daddy love her like Kaeleigh? Oh well, she has a lot more men wanting her.<br /><br />Hopkins writes a powerful story about child abuse in an upper-class family. The novel is written entirely in first-person free verse. The twins' internal dialogues and worries are very common to every teenager, although they are also warped and bent by the sex abuse. The intensity is extreme. A good outcome is not a sure bet. The sexual abuse leads to a lot of mental instability. Kaeleigh and Raeanne do things progressively more harsh to punish themselves. The punishment helps them stay in control to appear normal. Despite how the two girls are becoming more involved in drugs and other measures in attempts to distract from their downward spiral of despair, neither people or friends at school have any idea about what is happening. There are two big secrets I haven't revealed about Kaeleigh, but some readers guess these secrets before the end. <br /><br />Nonetheless, I think the book an excellent choice for young adults and mature teens to read. It shows so much of what really happens and the how and why victims of sexual abuse almost never go public. However, I think if a reader is a mature teen or close to being a mature young adult, especially sensitive or abused teens, they should have a responsible smart non-abusive kind adult available for guidance in reading this book, or to be there as a listener for younger readers to vent. <br /><br />It is terribly upsetting for adult people who know how often sex abuse happens unpunished, but exponentially worse for younger people inexperienced in how life works sometimes. It is a good thing that for some victims professional psychiatric help is available. Sometimes ordinary people can render temporary help until the professionals are available (or asked) to do something. But the first step is for people to learn what are the signs of abuse and what to expect if one decides to take any steps. The victim might not let you help her at all! So, gentle reader, news flash! life is complicated. This novel gives much insight to many of the issues surrounding the problem.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8598782792972439907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_517786697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/517786697" />
    <a title="Aryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6415628-aryn"><img alt="Aryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560285805p2/6415628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/517786697?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aryn" href="/user/show/6415628-aryn">Aryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6415628-aryn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6415628-aryn?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6415628-aryn?shelf=loaned-to-me">loaned-to-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer517786697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11798995325052247086"><b>Actual Rating: 1 and a half stars</b><br/>I was kind and rounded up.<br/><br/>I finished this book last night and I'm still not entirely certain what I want to say about it or how I want to rate it. I wanted to sleep on it, mull it over - I'm still at a loss. So, I'm just going to start writing and hope that whatever spills out gives me an appropriate star rating.<br/><br/>What the back of the book says: "Kaeleigh and Raeanne are identical down to the dimple. As daughters of a district-court judge father and a politician mo</span>
  <span id="freeText11798995325052247086" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 1 and a half stars</b><br>I was kind and rounded up.<br><br>I finished this book last night and I'm still not entirely certain what I want to say about it or how I want to rate it. I wanted to sleep on it, mull it over - I'm still at a loss. So, I'm just going to start writing and hope that whatever spills out gives me an appropriate star rating.<br><br>What the back of the book says: "Kaeleigh and Raeanne are identical down to the dimple. As daughters of a district-court judge father and a politician mother, they are an all-American family - on the surface. But behind the facade, each sister has her own dark secret."<br><br>First of all, during the entire book, I couldn't remember the girls' names, so I was calling them <b>Twin 1</b> and <b>Twin 2</b>. I'm probably just going to continue that into the review, because that'll let me have more of a stream of consciousness, try to get this all out. <br><br>Twin 1 is being raped by Daddy, and Twin 2 wants to be raped by Daddy. I almost had to stop reading on page 25. <br><blockquote>
  <i>"...And if Daddy would just stand<br>still for me, I'd happily tap his core."</i>
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406866ra/794226.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406866ra/794227.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I threw the book against the wall at that point and walked away. I was pissed, and honestly, I still am. That was a clue that perhaps this book was written for the shock value, and not entirely for tackling the issue. I know it's a hard issue to tackle, but I've read books with similar subject matters and none of them have left me with a book on the other side of the room and twitching. <b>Shock value is not synonymous with tackling difficult issues.</b> One of the reviews I read on Goodreads, that I can't find at the moment - if you find it, let me know and I'll link to it - called this book <b>"trauma porn."</b> At this point I am inclined to agree.<br><br>Thank Gods after that point the <i>I want to fuck Daddy,</i> erotic language was largely dropped, because that's what made it seem like Hopkins was just trying to get a rise out of us. There were definitely other scenes that I felt were written for their shock, rather than their value, but nothing that got such a disgusted reaction from me.<br><br>Twin 1 is the "weak" twin, who can't say no, is the lead in the school play (Grease). Twin 2 is the "strong" twin, getting stoned daily, sleeping around with her dealers. Both twins have eating disorders of various types, and deal with their pain in less-than-healthy ways. Mom is always away, she's running for Congress, only returning for photo-ops. Daddy's a judge and he's also an alcoholic, control freak.<br><br>It was almost a 600 page book, and I had the <b>big twist</b> figured out in the first 150 or so. I think if I hadn't figured it out, I would have stopped reading. It made some of the shock value stuff seem less out-and-out shock value. I'd explain why, but if you still plan to read this, or are reading it and haven't figured out the big twist, I won't give it away for you.<br><br>I think that Ellen Hopkins is an incredibly talented author, I actually enjoyed the prose - and I am not a poetry person, not even a little. What soured this book for me is that I didn't think she was actually tackling the big issue, I think she was writing to get a rise. And she got one, but not in a good way.<br><br>I think that I'd be interested to read Crank, because that was based on her daughter, so it will probably be less shock-value and more actual value.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11798995325052247086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13001208954711379745">This story is about two identical twins, Kaeleigh and Raeanne. Kaeleigh is being abused by her father and Raeanne is jealous of the attention she gets. It's messed up! The book goes through how each twin deals with the abuse and the additional problems that arise because of it. <br/><br/>It is hard for me to give a book about abuse 5 stars - I know, I know, the subject matter shouldn't really influence me like that especially since I chose to read it. This book was so well written though! Each twin's char</span>
  <span id="freeText13001208954711379745" style="display:none">This story is about two identical twins, Kaeleigh and Raeanne. Kaeleigh is being abused by her father and Raeanne is jealous of the attention she gets. It's messed up! The book goes through how each twin deals with the abuse and the additional problems that arise because of it. <br /><br />It is hard for me to give a book about abuse 5 stars - I know, I know, the subject matter shouldn't really influence me like that especially since I chose to read it. This book was so well written though! Each twin's character is well developed and unique. The story is horrifically messed up; I kept cringing through each chapter. And just things were building and I thought I knew what was going to happen, the author completely blew me away with a twist. It was amazing! So even though I really didn't like what happens in the story, I can't deny that it was an amazing book and deserves 5 stars. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6140388727661488808">Want to see more bookish things from me? Check out my YouTube Channel: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCferU-BCL2dlFjWdD0rS75Q/videos'>https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCfer...</a><br/><br/>Kaleigh and Raeanne are identical twins, each with their own dark secret.   <span id="freeText6140388727661488808" style="display:none">Want to see more bookish things from me? Check out my YouTube Channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCferU-BCL2dlFjWdD0rS75Q/videos">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCfer...</a><br /><br />Kaleigh and Raeanne are identical twins, each with their own dark secret. Raeanne quickly turns to drugs, sex and alcohol to try and fill the void her parents created. With each sister spiralling out of control, they need to save each other, before it's too late. <br /><br /><br />Wow... This book blew me away. This book is so twisted and dark, it had me on the edge of my seat the entire time. I had my theory on how the book would end, I ended up being correct, but honestly I thought it was so far fetched and didn't think that it would actually happen, but I'm so glad Hopkins decided to end it the way she did! I love the alternating perspectives between the two twins. This is my first Ellen Hopkins book and I can not wait to read more of her work!!! </span>

<div id="review_2383176931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2383176931" />
    <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling"><img alt="• Lindsey Dahling •" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578858809p2/26262267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2383176931?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lindsey Dahling •" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling">• Lindsey Dahling •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2383176931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18193152068755705730">This book was okay. It was fine. It was medium. Hopkins is notorious for luring her readers into dark, sensitive territories through poetic POVs of initially innocent, good-natured young women. I didn’t particularly care for this one, though. Identical seemed to go for shock value rather than any sort of complexity, so all of the characters felt highly generic regardless of the horrible abuse they suffered (and there is A LOT). Nothing ever went further than superficial. There is “cutting to fee</span>
  <span id="freeText18193152068755705730" style="display:none">This book was okay. It was fine. It was medium. Hopkins is notorious for luring her readers into dark, sensitive territories through poetic POVs of initially innocent, good-natured young women. I didn’t particularly care for this one, though. Identical seemed to go for shock value rather than any sort of complexity, so all of the characters felt highly generic regardless of the horrible abuse they suffered (and there is A LOT). Nothing ever went further than superficial. There is “cutting to feel pain” and “throwing up because it’s the only thing I can control” and all other cliche explanations for serious mental health disorders. As someone who has struggled with poor mental health since adolescence, I can assure you I never once had any idea why I was self-harming every night before bed. In fact, I remember listening to songs about the “I cut to feel” cliche on the school bus in 9th grade (the emo phase was big at the time, and while I was in no way an “emo” or “scene” kid, that didn’t stop me from enjoying some classic My Chemical Romance) and feeling even more isolated before I couldn’t identify with it at all. Mental health deserves better than generic, Hopkins.<br /><br />However, I do want to look at a small piece of Hopkins’s prose that I find highly relevant to the political world this week:<br /><br /><i>“I didn’t want him to go to prison.<br />He probably would have pulled <br />strings to avoid it, anyway. I didn’t <br />want to see him locked up. But<br />more, I didn’t want to testify.”</i><br /><br />Because testifying would mean reliving it. Reliving it in front of an audience. Reliving it in front of the world. Reliving it in front of <i>him</i>. And you don’t get to just relive it. <br /><br />No. <br /><br />Now you get to relive the soul-shattering agony tear you apart stitch by stitch under a spotlight of eyes that scream, <br /><br /><b>
  <i>It’s been decades...</i>
</b> <br /><br />and, <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Move on...</i>
</b> <br /><br />and, often with fatal results, <br /><br /><b>
  <i>We don’t believe you...</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18193152068755705730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Visit my <a href='http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a>!<br/><br/>This is not my first Ellen Hopkins book so I know by now not to expect fluffy bunnies and happily ever after endings.   <span id="freeText9502134707628928182" style="display:none">Interested in more of my reviews? Visit my <a href="http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>!<br /><br />This is not my first Ellen Hopkins book so I know by now not to expect fluffy bunnies and happily ever after endings. I know to expect a vivid depiction of exactly how life can be and is for some… but boy oh boy, this one really takes the cake. <br /><br />Identical is the story of Kaeleigh and Raeanne, 16 year-old identical twins. Their father is a district court judge and their mother is currently running for Congress. On the outside their family is picture perfect… but look closely and you’ll see the cracks in their veneer. Kaeleigh has been sexually abused by her father since she was nine years old. Raeanne drinks and uses drugs heavily because she feels she’s the lesser twin that isn’t loved like Kaeleigh. Their story is a stomach turning experience.<br /><br />I’m not sure I would have actually finished this if I didn't have faith in Ellen Hopkins to pull off one whopper of a story, and sure enough she did. The ending blew my mind and almost had me wanting to sit down and read it again because every notion or preconception I had was way off the mark. Brutal story but so incredibly well done it was shocking. </span>
