<div id="review_493355406" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/493355406" />
    <a title="NotoriousGOT" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4366666-notoriousgot"><img alt="NotoriousGOT" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364481379p2/4366666.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/493355406?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NotoriousGOT" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NotoriousGOT" href="/user/show/4366666-notoriousgot">NotoriousGOT</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416950066" href="/book/show/7775706-identical">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4366666-notoriousgot?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4366666-notoriousgot?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer493355406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4352724312234338184">2.5 stars for this one, but will round up to 3. While I found Ellen's writing hypnotic and it sucked me in, in a big way, I felt like this just seemed too....taboo. (Not going to lie. I figured out the plot twist by just reading the synopsis. )<br/><br/>I get that Ellen wants to tackle the very real problems of child molestation, pedophilia, drug abuse, mental illness....but it felt just very visceral and too much trying to shock you with horrific scenes. <br/><br/>I am no prude, but seriously, I can do without a s</span>
  <span id="freeText4352724312234338184" style="display:none">2.5 stars for this one, but will round up to 3. While I found Ellen's writing hypnotic and it sucked me in, in a big way, I felt like this just seemed too....taboo. (Not going to lie. I figured out the plot twist by just reading the synopsis. )<br /><br />I get that Ellen wants to tackle the very real problems of child molestation, pedophilia, drug abuse, mental illness....but it felt just very visceral and too much trying to shock you with horrific scenes. <br /><br />I am no prude, but seriously, I can do without a scene about a father performing oral sex on his 10 year old daughter. I got it. I got uncomfortable the first time she describes one of her fatherly encounters. I also got it on the second or third. <br /><br />What I wanted, what I hoped for, was for Ellen to address the protag's mental state AFTER she had finally decided to address her problems. I was so hoping for a story that would not only open your eyes to the horror of acts like child molestation, but then show readers (especially young readers who might personally identify with the story) that you can rise above something like that. That you can, as a teenager, heal your wounds.<br /><br />Instead, the ending is rushed and bleak. But it felt bleak as if Ellen had decided that since all of her other books have bleak endings, this one should have one too. I'm not asking for a happy ending, I just think that the more interesting story is watching someone go through something horrible like that and then figure out how to get to the other side.<br /><br /><br />Either way, I think Ellen Hopkins is an incredibly important writer and one every reader needs to explore. Does she have better books, probably. Would I recommend this to a first time Ellen Hopkins reader? Probably not. This was my first venture into her work and I feel like it just wasn't her best (based on the reviews and word of mouth thoughts on some of her other work.) <br /><br />Overall though, I am happy I finally read one of her books and this one is one I'm surely not to forget....ever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4352724312234338184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49573597" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49573597" />
    <a title="MarnieSkinner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2137304-marnieskinner"><img alt="MarnieSkinner" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49573597?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MarnieSkinner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MarnieSkinner" href="/user/show/2137304-marnieskinner">MarnieSkinner</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49573597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1329669256662752374">Reading the book <u>Identical</u> was a very different experience for me, in an imaginative sort of way. It was very disturbing to hear all of the problems each "girl" were going through; with their father, their mother, grandparents, Ian, and schooling. Everything happening in their lives was so dramatic, nothing seemed to be good for either of them. It hurt me to have to hear all their complaints, espeically when it came to Kaeleigh. Every turn of the page was very suspenceful, knowing and waiting fo</span>
  <span id="freeText1329669256662752374" style="display:none">Reading the book <u>Identical</u> was a very different experience for me, in an imaginative sort of way. It was very disturbing to hear all of the problems each "girl" were going through; with their father, their mother, grandparents, Ian, and schooling. Everything happening in their lives was so dramatic, nothing seemed to be good for either of them. It hurt me to have to hear all their complaints, espeically when it came to Kaeleigh. Every turn of the page was very suspenceful, knowing and waiting for some new twisted situation to occur. Over all the book was very overwelming. It made me think of awful things, it also gave me the feeling of sadness; I actually felt connected to the girls throughout the entire book. Many emotions raced in and out of my mind as I read. Towards the end of the book is where everything started getting jumbled together. It came so fast without any clues, it was sort of like the auther just threw it in there, just as a way to end the book quicker, which I did not like at all. The end of the book was very confusing and suprising, it all happened so sudden I didn't have time to process what was happening.<br /><br />When reading <u>Identical</u> I actually learned quite a bit. It showed me that people can be very diceiving, even those who are close to you and at times you might not be able to trust them. It taught me that insest and things of that nature happen more often then expected or hoped. I look at a lot of things differently; my home life and my social life. I appreciate what I have, opposed to what it could be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1329669256662752374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/653951810?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janie Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janie Johnson" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson">Janie Johnson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=2013-challenge">2013-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=ellen-hopkins">ellen-hopkins</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer653951810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6054378336804022743">I was looking for a quick fluid read to end this month with and I am so glad I picked up this one. Wow, another great work of art by Ellen Hopkins. Whenever I read her stuff I am forced to feel! I experience a huge variety of emotions, from hatred to disgust to love and sadness. I can't help myself really, her words draw me to tears every time I read her works. She writes with such raw emotion, you can't help but feel everything she feels, everything her characters feel.<br/><br/>From the start you are le</span>
  <span id="freeText6054378336804022743" style="display:none">I was looking for a quick fluid read to end this month with and I am so glad I picked up this one. Wow, another great work of art by Ellen Hopkins. Whenever I read her stuff I am forced to feel! I experience a huge variety of emotions, from hatred to disgust to love and sadness. I can't help myself really, her words draw me to tears every time I read her works. She writes with such raw emotion, you can't help but feel everything she feels, everything her characters feel.<br /><br />From the start you are let inside of Kayleigh's and Raeanne's heads and their messed up lives. I could never even imagine living a life such as this. I felt as though I jumped right into the book and lived these lives with them, powerless to help them or heal them. No one to really talk to or ask for help. They had to handle all the craziness in their lives themselves. Their parents are a prime example of what is wrong with this world today.<br /><br />I like Hopkins style of writing too and that is due to being a poet myself. Her words flow with so much meaning. The reading is so fluid. So much so that it makes it hard to put the book down. I would recommend this book or actually all her books to anyone. Even though she writes in verse her novels speak volumes and everyone should at least try her out and see what they can discover and feel as well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6054378336804022743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PVXMTHw1cI5lnnU2jZ6Ft3/1eAve10j42akzgL4MAJDjQCLoGTiYqAad1PclyZfwPrsj1BgbXJ7O1rFA60cZYQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7O6QPTMvQ+HNQJ3PC8SzAJUEVszXOEWmvhkDvBkuJh0y+36ZViKrx65DPA6jk6FH1EoNExH0UcCpZoF8TGU/7A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer15850924303483461533"><i>Ellen Hopkins</i> is the New York Times bestselling author of <i>Crank</i>, <i>Burned</i>, <i>Impulse</i>, <i>Glass</i>, <i>Identical</i>, <i>Tricks</i>, <i>Fallout</i>, <i>Perfect</i>, <i>Triangles</i>, <i>Tilt</i>, and <i>Collateral</i>. She lives in Carson City, Nevada, with her husband and son. Hopkin's Facebook, Twitter, Tumblr and Pinterest pages get thousands of hits from teens who claim Hopkins is the "only one who understands me", and she can be visited at ellenhopkin</span>
  <span id="freeText15850924303483461533" style="display:none"><i>Ellen Hopkins</i> is the New York Times bestselling author of <i>Crank</i>, <i>Burned</i>, <i>Impulse</i>, <i>Glass</i>, <i>Identical</i>, <i>Tricks</i>, <i>Fallout</i>, <i>Perfect</i>, <i>Triangles</i>, <i>Tilt</i>, and <i>Collateral</i>. She lives in Carson City, Nevada, with her husband and son. Hopkin's Facebook, Twitter, Tumblr and Pinterest pages get thousands of hits from teens who claim Hopkins is the "only one who understands me", and she can be visited at ellenhopkins.com. <br /><br />Like most of you here, books are my life. Reading is a passion, but writing is the biggest part of me. Balance is my greatest challenge, as I love my family, friends, animals and home, but also love traveling to meet my readers. Hope I meet many of you soon!</span>
